class="mediawiki ltr sitedir-ltr mw-hide-empty-elt ns-0 ns-subject page-Typhon rootpage-Typhon vector-experimental-print-styles vector-nav-directionality skin-vector action-view"> <div class="noprint" CentralNotice --></div>\n<div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n</div>\n<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Typhon</h1>\n<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">\n<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\n<div id="contentSub"></div>\n<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">\n\t\t\t\t\tJump to:\t\t\t\t\t<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, \t\t\t\t\t<a href="#p-search">search</a>\n</div>\n<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">This article is about Typhon in Greek mythology. For other uses, see <a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Typhon_(disambiguation)" title="Typhon (disambiguation)">Typhon (disambiguation)</a>.</div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Zeus_Typhon_Staatliche_Antikensammlungen_596.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1264" data-file-width="2016" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Zeus_Typhon_Staatliche_Antikensammlungen_596.jpg/280px-Zeus_Typhon_Staatliche_Antikensammlungen_596.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Zeus_Typhon_Staatliche_Antikensammlungen_596.jpg/420px-Zeus_Typhon_Staatliche_Antikensammlungen_596.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Zeus_Typhon_Staatliche_Antikensammlungen_596.jpg/560px-Zeus_Typhon_Staatliche_Antikensammlungen_596.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Zeus_Typhon_Staatliche_Antikensammlungen_596.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Zeus" title="Zeus">Zeus</a> aiming his thunderbolt at a winged and snake-footed Typhon. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chalcidia" title="Chalcidia">Chalcidian</a> black-figured <a href="/wiki/Hydria" title="Hydria">hydria</a> (c. 540\xe2\x80\x93530 BC), <a href="/wiki/Staatliche_Antikensammlungen" title="Staatliche Antikensammlungen">Staatliche Antikensammlungen</a> (Inv. 596).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p><b>Typhon</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="\'t\' in \'tie\'">t</span><span title="/a\xc9\xaa/: \'i\' in \'tide\'">a\xc9\xaa</span><span title="\'f\' in \'find\'">f</span><span title="/\xc9\x92/: \'o\' in \'body\'">\xc9\x92</span><span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">n</span></span>, -<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="\'f\' in \'find\'">f</span><span title="/\xc9\x99n/: \'on\' in \'button\'">\xc9\x99n</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el" xml:lang="el">\xce\xa4\xcf\x85\xcf\x86\xe1\xbf\xb6\xce\xbd</span>, <i>Tuph\xc5\x8dn</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Greek" title="Help:IPA/Greek">[typ\xca\xb0\xc9\x94\xcc\x82\xcb\x90n]</a></span>), also <b>Typhoeus</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="\'t\' in \'tie\'">t</span><span title="/a\xc9\xaa/: \'i\' in \'tide\'">a\xc9\xaa</span><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="\'f\' in \'find\'">f</span><span title="/i\xcb\x90/: \'ee\' in \'fleece\'">i\xcb\x90</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: \'a\' in \'about\'">\xc9\x99</span><span title="\'s\' in \'sigh\'">s</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <span lang="el" xml:lang="el">\xce\xa4\xcf\x85\xcf\x86\xcf\x89\xce\xb5\xcf\x8d\xcf\x82</span>, <i>Tuph\xc5\x8deus</i>), <b>Typhaon</b> (<span lang="el" xml:lang="el">\xce\xa4\xcf\x85\xcf\x86\xce\xac\xcf\x89\xce\xbd</span>, <i>Tupha\xc5\x8dn</i>) or <b>Typhos</b> (<span lang="el" xml:lang="el">\xce\xa4\xcf\x85\xcf\x86\xcf\x8e\xcf\x82</span>, <i>Tuph\xc5\x8ds</i>), was a monstrous serpentine giant and the most deadly creature in <a href="/wiki/Greek_mythology" title="Greek mythology">Greek mythology</a>. According to <a href="/wiki/Hesiod" title="Hesiod">Hesiod</a>, Typhon was the son of <a href="/wiki/Gaia_(mythology)" title="Gaia (mythology)">Gaia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tartarus" title="Tartarus">Tartarus</a>. However one source has Typhon as the son of <a href="/wiki/Hera" title="Hera">Hera</a> alone, while another makes Typhon the offspring of <a href="/wiki/Cronus" title="Cronus">Cronus</a>. Typhon and his mate <a href="/wiki/Echidna_(mythology)" title="Echidna (mythology)">Echidna</a> were the progenitors of many famous monsters.</p>\n<p>Typhon attempted to overthrow <a href="/wiki/Zeus" title="Zeus">Zeus</a> for the supremacy of the cosmos. The two fought a cataclysmic battle, which Zeus finally won with the aid of his thunderbolts. Defeated, Typhon was cast into Tartarus, or buried underneath Mount Etna, or the island of <a href="/wiki/Ischia" title="Ischia">Ischia</a>.</p>\n<p>Typhon mythology is part of the Greek succession myth, which explained how Zeus came to rule the gods. Typhon\'s story is also connected with that of Python (the serpent killed by <a href="/wiki/Apollo" title="Apollo">Apollo</a>), and both stories probably derived from several Near Eastern antecedents. Typhon was (from c. 500 BC) also identified with the Egyptian god of destruction <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Set_(mythology)" title="Set (mythology)">Set</a>. In later accounts Typhon was often confused with the <a href="/wiki/Giants_(Greek_mythology)" title="Giants (Greek mythology)">Giants</a>.</p>\n<p></p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc">\n<div
